# Kubernetes Controller Runtime Reconciler Registration

## Your Task

Trace how a controller registers itself with the controller-runtime Manager in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find the Go source files that define the Reconciler interface, implement SetupWithManager, and wire the controller into the manager's reconcile loop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:


Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

   402→
   403→// IsControllerEnabled checks if the context's controllers enabled or not
   404→func (c ControllerContext) IsControllerEnabled(controllerDescriptor *ControllerDescriptor) bool {
   405→	controllersDisabledByDefault := sets.NewString()
   406→	if controllerDescriptor.IsDisabledByDefault() {
   407→		controllersDisabledByDefault.Insert(controllerDescriptor.Name())
   408→	}
   409→	return genericcontrollermanager.IsControllerEnabled(controllerDescriptor.Name(), controllersDisabledByDefault, c.ComponentConfig.Generic.Controllers)
   410→}
   411→
   412→// InitFunc is used to launch a particular controller. It returns a controller
   413→// that can optionally implement other interfaces so that the controller manager
   414→// can support the requested features.
   415→// The returned controller may be nil, which will be considered an anonymous controller
   416→// that requests no additional features from the controller manager.
   417→// Any error returned will cause the controller process to `Fatal`
   418→// The bool indicates whether the controller was enabled.
   419→type InitFunc func(ctx context.Context, controllerContext ControllerContext, controllerName string) (controller controller.Interface, enabled bool, err error)
   420→
   421→type ControllerDescriptor struct {
   422→	name                      string
   423→	initFunc                  InitFunc
   424→	requiredFeatureGates      []featuregate.Feature
   425→	aliases                   []string
   426→	isDisabledByDefault       bool
   427→	isCloudProviderController bool
   428→	requiresSpecialHandling   bool
   429→}
   430→
   431→func (r *ControllerDescriptor) Name() string {
   432→	return r.name
   433→}

Perfect! I now have comprehensive information. Let me compile my findings:

## Summary: Reconciler Interface, SetupWithManager, and Controller-Runtime Patterns

Based on my search through the Kubernetes codebase, here are the key findings regarding controller-runtime patterns:

### 1. **Reconciler Interface Definition**

While the workspace doesn't contain the actual `sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime` library (it's not vendored in Kubernetes 1.32.0), the pattern is evident in Kubernetes' own implementations:

**Pattern from `k8s.io/endpointslice`:**
```go
// File: /workspace/kubernetes--v1.32.0/staging/src/k8s.io/endpointslice/reconciler.go
type Reconciler struct {
    client               clientset.Interface
    nodeLister           corelisters.NodeLister
    maxEndpointsPerSlice int32
    // ... other fields
}

// Reconcile method for transforming current state into desired state
func (r *Reconciler) Reconcile(logger klog.Logger, service *corev1.Service, pods []*corev1.Pod, 
    existingSlices []*discovery.EndpointSlice, triggerTime time.Time) error
```

**Controller-runtime library pattern** (not in workspace but referenced):
- The library defines a `Reconciler` interface with a `Reconcile` method that takes:
  - Context
  - Request (typically containing object name/namespace)
  - Returns Result and error

Perfect! I've completed the tracing of how controllers register themselves with the controller manager in Kubernetes. I've created a comprehensive analysis at `/workspace/answer.json` with the following findings:

## Summary

The answer documents how controllers register with the Kubernetes controller manager using the `k8s.io/controller-manager` library architecture. Key findings include:

### Core Components

1. **Controller Interface** - Defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go`, with optional `Debuggable` and `HealthCheckable` interfaces

2. **ControllerDescriptor** - The registration pattern in Kubernetes (located in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` at line 421-429) that holds:
   - Controller name and aliases
   - InitFunc (the equivalent of `SetupWithManager` in controller-runtime)
   - Feature gate requirements

3. **InitFunc** - The core registration function (line 419 in controllermanager.go) that:
   - Creates controller instances
   - Registers informer event handlers
   - Starts worker goroutines

4. **ControllerContext** - A dependency injection container providing:
   - ClientBuilder for API clients
   - InformerFactory for shared informers
   - Configuration and REST mapper

### Registration Chain

The flow follows: `Run()` → `NewControllerDescriptors()` → `CreateControllerContext()` → `StartControllers()` → individual `InitFunc` implementations

### Key Files

- **staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go** - Controller interface definitions
- **cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go** - Manager and registration logic
- **staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go** - Example complete controller implementation
- **staging/src/k8s.io/endpointslice/reconcile

This reconciles state for the attach/detach controller. That\n// reconciles state for the kubelet volume manager.\ntype Reconciler interface {\n\t// Starts running the reconciliation loop which executes periodically, checks\n\t// if volumes that should be attached are attached and volumes that should\n\t// be detached are detached. If during this time the volume\n// becomes used by a new pod, the detach request will be aborted and the timer\n// cleared.\nfunc NewReconciler(\n\tloopPeriod corelisters.NodeLister,\n\trecorder record.EventRecorder) Reconciler {\n\treturn &reconciler{\n\t\tloopPeriod:                  loopPeriod,\n\t\tmaxWaitForUnmountDuration:   maxWaitForUnmountDuration,\n\t\tsyncDuration:                syncDuration,\n\t\tdisableReconciliationSync:   disableReconciliationSync,\n\t\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout: attacherDetacher,\n\t\tnodeStatusUpdater:           nodeStatusUpdater,\n\t\tnodeLister:                  nodeLister,\n\t\ttimeOfLastSync:              time.Now(),\n\t\trecorder: time.Time\n\tdisableReconciliationSync   bool\n\tdisableForceDetachOnTimeout bool\n\trecorder                    record.EventRecorder\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n\twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, rc.reconciliationLoopFunc(ctx), rc.loopPeriod)\n}\n\n// reconciliationLoopFunc this can be disabled via cli option disableReconciliation.\n// It periodically checks whether the attached volumes from actual state\n// are still attached to the node and update the status if they are not.\nfunc (rc *reconciler) reconciliationLoopFunc(ctx context.Context) func(context.Context) {\n\treturn func(ctx context.Context) {\n\n\t\trc.reconcile(ctx)\n\t\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\t\tif rc.disableReconciliationSync {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Skipping reconciling attached volumes still attached since it is disabled via the command line\")\n\t\t} else if rc.syncDuration < time.Second {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Skipping reconciling attached volumes still attached since it is set to less than one second via the command line\")\n\t\t} else if time.Since(rc.timeOfLastSync) > rc.syncDuration {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Starting reconciling attached volumes still attached\")\n\t\t\trc.sync()\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) sync() {\n\tdefer rc.updateSyncTime()\n\trc.syncStates()\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) updateSyncTime() {\n\trc.timeOfLastSync = time.Now()\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) syncStates() {\n\tvolumesPerNode := rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachedVolumesPerNode()\n\trc.attacherDetacher.VerifyVolumesAreAttached(volumesPerNode, rc.actualStateOfWorld)\n}\n\n// hasOutOfServiceTaint returns true if the node has out-of-service taint present.\nfunc (rc *reconciler) hasOutOfServiceTaint(nodeName types.NodeName) (bool, error) {\n\tnode, err := rc.nodeLister.Get(string(nodeName))\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nodeIsHealthy(nodeName types.NodeName) (bool, error) {\n\tnode, err := rc.nodeLister.Get(string(nodeName))\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn false, err\n\t}\n\treturn nodeutil.IsNodeReady(node), nil\n}\n\nfunc (rc *reconciler) reconcile(ctx context.Context) {\n\t// Detaches are triggered before attaches so that volumes referenced by\n\t// pods that are rescheduled to a different node are detached first.\n\n\t// Ensure volumes that should be detached are detached.\n\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\tfor _, attachedVolume := range rc.actualStateOfWorld.GetAttachedVolumes() {\n\t\tif !rc.desiredStateOfWorld.VolumeExists(\n\t\t\tattachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName) {\n\n\t\t\t// Check whether there already exist an operation pending, and don't even\n\t\t\t// try to operationexecutor.DetachOperationName) {\n\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running or still in exponential backoff for node. Can't start detach\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tif !rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationSafeToRetry(attachedVolume.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, \"\" /* nodeName */, operationexecutor.DetachOperationName) {\n\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running or still in exponential backoff in the cluster. whether the umount drain timer expired\n\t\t\tmaxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired := elapsedTime > rc.maxWaitForUnmountDuration\n\n\t\t\tisHealthy, err := rc.nodeIsHealthy(attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to get health of node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Force detach volumes from unhealthy nodes after maxWaitForUnmountDuration if force detach is enabled\n\t\t\t// Ensure that the timeout condition checks this correctly so that the correct metric is updated below\n\t\t\tforceDetatchTimeoutExpired := maxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired && !rc.disableForceDetachOnTimeout\n\t\t\tif maxWaitForUnmountDurationExpired && rc.disableForceDetachOnTimeout {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Drain timeout expired for volume but disableForceDetachOnTimeout was set\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tforceDetach := !isHealthy && forceDetatchTimeoutExpired\n\n\t\t\thasOutOfServiceTaint, err := rc.hasOutOfServiceTaint(attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to get taint specs for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Check whether volume is still mounted. Skip detach if it is still mounted unless we have\n\t\t\t// decided to force detach or the node has `node.kubernetes.io/out-of-service` taint.\n\t\t\tif attachedVolume.MountedByNode && !forceDetach && !hasOutOfServiceTaint {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Cannot detach volume because it is still mounted\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Before triggering volume detach, mark volume as detached and update the node status\n\t\t\t// If it fails to update node status, skip information.\n\t\t\terr = rc.actualStateOfWorld.RemoveVolumeFromReportAsAttached(attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"RemoveVolumeFromReportAsAttached failed while removing volume from node\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)),\n\t\t\t\t\t\"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName,\n\t\t\t\t\t\"err\", err)\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Update Node Status to indicate volume is no longer safe to mount.\n\t\t\terr = rc.nodeStatusUpdater.UpdateNodeStatusForNode(logger, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t// Skip detaching this volume if unable to update node status\n\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"UpdateNodeStatusForNode failed while attempting to report volume as attached\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t// Add volume back to ReportAsAttached if UpdateNodeStatusForNode call failed so that node status updater will add it back to VolumeAttached list.\n\t\t\t\t// It is needed here too because DetachVolume is not call actually and we keep the data consistency for every reconcile.\n\t\t\t\trc.actualStateOfWorld.AddVolumeToReportAsAttached(logger, attachedVolume.VolumeName, attachedVolume.NodeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Trigger detach volume which requires verifying safe to detach step\n\t\t\t// If forceDetatchTimeoutExpired is true, skip verifySafeToDetach check\n\t\t\t// If the node has node.kubernetes.io/out-of-service taint with NoExecute effect, skip verifySafeToDetach check\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Starting attacherDetacher.DetachVolume\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\tif hasOutOfServiceTaint {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"node has out-of-service taint\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tverifySafeToDetach := !(forceDetatchTimeoutExpired || hasOutOfServiceTaint)\n\t\t\terr = rc.attacherDetacher.DetachVolume(logger, attachedVolume.AttachedVolume, verifySafeToDetach, rc.actualStateOfWorld)\n\t\t\tif err == nil {\n\t\t\t\tif verifySafeToDetach { // normal detach\n\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume started\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t} else { // force detach\n\t\t\t\t\tif forceDetatchTimeoutExpired {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tmetrics.RecordForcedDetachMetric(metrics.ForceDetachReasonTimeout)\n\t\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume started: this volume is not safe to detach, but {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tmetrics.RecordForcedDetachMetric(metrics.ForceDetachReasonOutOfService)\n\t\t\t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"attacherDetacher.DetachVolume started: node has out-of-service taint, force detaching\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(attachedVolume.NodeName)),\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"volumeName\", attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t// Add volume back to ReportAsAttached if DetachVolume call failed so that node status updater will add it back to VolumeAttached list.\n\t\t\t\t// This function is also called during attachedVolume.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\trc.attachDesiredVolumes(logger)\n\n\t// Update Node Status\n\terr := rc.nodeStatusUpdater.UpdateNodeStatuses(logger)\n\tif err != nil if there is already one running for the given volume and node.\n\t\t\tif rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationPending(volumeToAttach.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, volumeToAttach.NodeName) {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running for node. Can't start attach\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(volumeToAttach.NodeName)), \"volumeName\", volumeToAttach.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t// Don't even try to start an operation if there is already one running for the given volume\n\t\t\tif rc.attacherDetacher.IsOperationPending(volumeToAttach.VolumeName, \"\" /* podName */, \"\" /* nodeName */) {\n\t\t\t\tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Operation for volume is already running. Can't start attach for node\", \"node\", klog.KRef(\"\", string(volumeToAttach.NodeName)), \"volumeNames\", volumeToAttach.VolumeName)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Because the attach already attached to different node(s).\nfunc (rc *reconciler) reportMultiAttachError(logger klog.Logger, volumeToAttach cache.VolumeToAttach, nodes []types.NodeName) {\n\t// Filter out the current slicesToUpdate, slicesToDelete))\n\t} else {\n\t\tr.metricsCache.UpdateTrafficDistributionForService(serviceNN, nil)\n\t}\n\n\terr := r.finalize(service, slicesToCreate, slicesToUpdate, slicesToDelete, triggerTime)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\terrs = append(errs, err)\n\t}\n\tfor _, event := range events {\n\t\tr.eventRecorder.Event(service, event.EventType, event.Reason, event.Message)\n\t}\n\treturn utilerrors.NewAggregate(errs)\n\n}\n\nfunc NewReconciler(client clientset.Interface, nodeLister corelisters.NodeLister, maxEndpointsPerSlice int32, endpointSliceTracker *endpointsliceutil.EndpointSliceTracker, topologyCache *topologycache.TopologyCache, eventRecorder record.EventRecorder, controllerName string, options ...ReconcilerOption) *Reconciler {\n\tr := &Reconciler{\n\t\tclient:               client,\n\t\tnodeLister:           nodeLister,\n\t\tmaxEndpointsPerSlice: maxEndpointsPerSlice,\n\t\tendpointSliceTracker: endpointSliceTracker,\n\t\tmetricsCache:         metrics.NewCache(maxEndpointsPerSlice),\n\t\ttopologyCache:        topologyCache,\n\t\teventRecorder:        eventRecorder,\n\t\tcontrollerName:       controllerName,\n\t}\n\tfor _, option := range options {\n\t\toption(r)\n\t}\n\treturn r\n}\n\n// placeholderSliceCompare is a conversion func for comparing two placeholder endpoint slices.\n// It only compares the specific fields we care about.\nvar placeholderSliceCompare = conversion.EqualitiesOrDie(\n\tfunc(a, b metav1.OwnerReference) bool {\n\t\treturn a.String() == b.String()\n\t},\n\tfunc(a, b metav1.ObjectMeta) bool {\n\t\tif a.Namespace != b.Namespace {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t\tfor k, v := range a.Labels {\n\t\t\tif b.Labels[k] != v {\n\t\t\t\treturn If there are slices to create and delete, change the creates to updates\n\t// of the slices that would otherwise be deleted.\n\tfor i := 0; i < len(slicesToDelete); {\n\t\tif len(slicesToCreate) == 0 {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t\tsliceToDelete := slicesToDelete[i]\n\t\tslice := slicesToCreate[len(slicesToCreate)-1]\n\t\t// Only update EndpointSlices that are owned by this Service and have\n\t\t// the same AddressType. We need to avoid updating EndpointSlices that\n\t\t// are being garbage collected for an old Service with the same name.\n\t\t// The AddressType field is immutable. Since Services also consider\n\t\t// IPFamily immutable, the only case where this should matter will be\n\t\t// the migration from IP to IPv4 and IPv6 AddressTypes, where there's a\n\t\t// chance EndpointSlices with an IP AddressType would otherwise be\n\t\t// updated to IPv4 or IPv6 without this check.\n\t\tif sliceToDelete.AddressType == slice.AddressType && ownedBy(sliceToDelete, service) {\n\t\t\tslice.Name = sliceToDelete.Name\n\t\t\tslicesToCreate = slicesToCreate[:len(slicesToCreate)-1]\n\t\t\tslicesToUpdate = append(slicesToUpdate, slice)\n\t\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete[:i], slicesToDelete[i+1:]...)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\ti++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Don't create new EndpointSlices if the Service is pending deletion. This\n\t// is to avoid a potential race condition with the garbage collector where\n\t// it tries to delete EndpointSlices as this controller replaces them.\n\tif service.DeletionTimestamp == nil {\n\t\tfor _, endpointSlice := range slicesToCreate {\n\t\t\taddTriggerTimeAnnotation(endpointSlice, triggerTime)\n\t\t\tcreatedSlice, err := r.client.DiscoveryV1().EndpointSlices(service.Namespace).Create(context.TODO(), endpointSlice, metav1.CreateOptions{})\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t// If the namespace is terminating, creates will continue to fail. Simply drop the item.\n\t\t\t\tif errors.HasStatusCause(err, corev1.NamespaceTerminatingCause) {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to create EndpointSlice for metav1.UpdateOptions{})\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to update %s EndpointSlice for Service %s/%s: %v\", endpointSlice.Name, service.Namespace, service.Name, err)\n\t\t}\n\t\tr.endpointSliceTracker.Update(updatedSlice)\n\t\tmetrics.EndpointSliceChanges.WithLabelValues(\"update\").Inc()\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, endpointSlice := range slicesToDelete {\n\t\terr := r.client.DiscoveryV1().EndpointSlices(service.Namespace).Delete(context.TODO(), endpointSlice.Name, metav1.DeleteOptions{})\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to delete %s err)\n\t\t}\n\t\tr.endpointSliceTracker.ExpectDeletion(endpointSlice)\n\t\tmetrics.EndpointSliceChanges.WithLabelValues(\"delete\").Inc()\n\t}\n\n\ttopologyLabel := \"Disabled\"\n\tif r.topologyCache != nil && hintsEnabled(service.Annotations) {\n\t\ttopologyLabel = \"Auto\"\n\t}\n\tvar trafficDistribution string\n\tif r.trafficDistributionEnabled && !hintsEnabled(service.Annotations) {\n\t\tif service.Spec.TrafficDistribution != nil && *service.Spec.TrafficDistribution == corev1.ServiceTrafficDistributionPreferClose {\n\t\t\ttrafficDistribution = len(slicesToDelete)\n\tmetrics.EndpointSlicesChangedPerSync.WithLabelValues(topologyLabel, trafficDistribution).Observe(float64(numSlicesChanged))\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// reconcileByPortMapping compares the endpoints found in existing slices with\n// the list of desired endpoints and returns lists of slices to create, update,\n// and delete. It also checks that the slices mirror the parent services labels.\n// The logic is split up into several main steps:\n//  1. Iterate through existing slices, delete endpoints that are no longer\n//     desired and update matching endpoints that have changed. It also checks\n//     if the slices have the labels of the parent services, and updates them if not.\n//  2. Iterate through slices that have been modified in 1 and fill them up with\n//     any remaining desired endpoints.\n//  3. If there still desired endpoints left, try to fit them into a previously\n//     unchanged slice and/or create new ones.\nfunc (r *Reconciler) reconcileByPortMapping(\n\tlogger klog.Logger,\n\tservice *corev1.Service,\n\texistingSlices []*discovery.EndpointSlice,\n\tdesiredSet endpointsliceutil.EndpointSet,\n\tendpointMeta *endpointMeta,\n) ([]*discovery.EndpointSlice, []*discovery.EndpointSlice, []*discovery.EndpointSlice, int, int) {\n\tslicesByName := map[string]*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n\tsliceNamesUnchanged := sets.New[string]()\n\tsliceNamesToUpdate := sets.New[string]()\n\tsliceNamesToDelete := sets.New[string]()\n\tnumRemoved := 0\n\n\t// 1. Iterate through existing slices to delete endpoints no longer desired\n\t//    and update endpoints that have changed\n\tfor _, existingSlice := range existingSlices {\n\t\tslicesByName[existingSlice.Name] = existingSlice\n\t\tnewEndpoints := []discovery.Endpoint{}\n\t\tendpointUpdated := false\n\t\tfor _, endpoint := range existingSlice.Endpoints {\n\t\t\tgot := desiredSet.Get(&endpoint)\n\t\t\t// If endpoint is desired add it to list of endpoints to keep.\n\t\t\tif got != nil {\n\t\t\t\tnewEndpoints = append(newEndpoints, *got)\n\t\t\t\t// If existing version of endpoint doesn't match desired version\n\t\t\t\t// set endpointUpdated to ensure endpoint changes are persisted.\n\t\t\t\tif !endpointsliceutil.EndpointsEqualBeyondHash(got, &endpoint) {\n\t\t\t\t\tendpointUpdated = true\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t// once an endpoint has been placed/found in a slice, it no\n\t\t\t\t// longer needs to be handled\n\t\t\t\tdesiredSet.Delete(&endpoint)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// generate the slice labels and check if parent labels have changed\n\t\tlabels, labelsChanged := setEndpointSliceLabels(logger, existingSlice, service, r.controllerName)\n\n\t\t// If an endpoint was updated or removed, mark for update or delete\n\t\tif endpointUpdated || len(existingSlice.Endpoints) != len(newEndpoints) {\n\t\t\tif len(existingSlice.Endpoints) > len(newEndpoints) {\n\t\t\t\tnumRemoved += len(existingSlice.Endpoints) - len(newEndpoints)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif len(newEndpoints) == 0 {\n\t\t\t\t// if no endpoints desired in this slice, mark for deletion\n\t\t\t\tsliceNamesToDelete.Insert(existingSlice.Name)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// otherwise, copy and mark for update\n\t\t\t\tepSlice := existingSlice.DeepCopy()\n\t\t\t\tepSlice.Endpoints = newEndpoints\n\t\t\t\tepSlice.Labels = labels\n\t\t\t\tslicesByName[existingSlice.Name] = epSlice\n\t\t\t\tsliceNamesToUpdate.Insert(epSlice.Name)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else if labelsChanged {\n\t\t\t// if labels have changed, copy and mark for update\n\t\t\tepSlice := existingSlice.DeepCopy()\n\t\t\tepSlice.Labels = labels\n\t\t\tslicesByName[existingSlice.Name] = epSlice\n\t\t\tsliceNamesToUpdate.Insert(epSlice.Name)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t// slices with no changes will be useful if there are leftover endpoints\n\t\t\tsliceNamesUnchanged.Insert(existingSlice.Name)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tnumAdded := desiredSet.Len()\n\n\t// 2. If we still have desired endpoints to add and slices marked for update,\n\t//    iterate through the slices and fill them up with the desired endpoints.\n\tif desiredSet.Len() > 0 && sliceNamesToUpdate.Len() > 0 {\n\t\tslices := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n\t\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesToUpdate.UnsortedList() {\n\t\t\tslices = append(slices, slicesByName[sliceName])\n\t\t}\n\t\t// Sort endpoint slices by length so we're filling up the fullest ones\n\t\t// first.\n\t\tsort.Sort(endpointSliceEndpointLen(slices))\n\n\t\t// Iterate through slices and fill them up with desired endpoints.\n\t\tfor _, slice := range slices {\n\t\t\tfor desiredSet.Len() > 0 && len(slice.Endpoints) < int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice) {\n\t\t\t\tendpoint, _ := desiredSet.PopAny()\n\t\t\t\tslice.Endpoints = append(slice.Endpoints, *endpoint)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// 3. If there are still desired endpoints left at this point, we try to fit\n\t//    the endpoints in a single existing slice. If there are no slices with\n\t//    that capacity, we create new slices for the endpoints.\n\tslicesToCreate := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n\n\tfor desiredSet.Len() > 0 {\n\t\tvar sliceToFill *discovery.EndpointSlice\n\n\t\t// If the remaining amounts of endpoints is smaller than the max\n\t\t// endpoints per slice and we have slices that haven't already been\n\t\t// filled, try to fit them in one.\n\t\tif desiredSet.Len() < int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice) && sliceNamesUnchanged.Len() > 0 {\n\t\t\tunchangedSlices := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n\t\t\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesUnchanged.UnsortedList() {\n\t\t\t\tunchangedSlices = append(unchangedSlices, slicesByName[sliceName])\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tsliceToFill = getSliceToFill(unchangedSlices, desiredSet.Len(), int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice))\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// If we didn't find a sliceToFill, generate a new empty one.\n\t\tif sliceToFill == nil {\n\t\t\tsliceToFill = newEndpointSlice(logger, service, endpointMeta, r.controllerName)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t// deep copy required to modify this slice.\n\t\t\tsliceToFill = sliceToFill.DeepCopy()\n\t\t\tslicesByName[sliceToFill.Name] = sliceToFill\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Fill the slice up with remaining endpoints.\n\t\tfor desiredSet.Len() > 0 && len(sliceToFill.Endpoints) < int(r.maxEndpointsPerSlice) {\n\t\t\tendpoint, _ := an update or create.\n\t\tif sliceToFill.Name != \"\" {\n\t\t\tsliceNamesToUpdate.Insert(sliceToFill.Name)\n\t\t\tsliceNamesUnchanged.Delete(sliceToFill.Name)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tslicesToCreate = sliceNamesToUpdate.UnsortedList() {\n\t\tslicesToUpdate = append(slicesToUpdate, slicesByName[sliceName])\n\t}\n\n\t// Build slicesToDelete from slice names.\n\tslicesToDelete := []*discovery.EndpointSlice{}\n\tfor _, sliceName := range sliceNamesToDelete.UnsortedList() {\n\t\tslicesToDelete = append(slicesToDelete, slicesByName[sliceName])\n\t}\n\n\treturn slicesToCreate, ownerRef != nil {\n   368\u2192\t\t// If this object is not owned by a Foo, we should not do anything more\n   369\u2192\t\t// with it.\n   370\u2192\t\tif ownerRef.Kind != \"Foo\" {\n   371\u2192\t\t\treturn\n   372\u2192\t\t}\n   373\u2192\n   374\u2192\t\tfoo, err := c.foosLister.Foos(object.GetNamespace()).Get(ownerRef.Name)\n   375\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   376\u2192\t\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"Ignore orphaned object\", \"object\", klog.KObj(object), \"foo\", ownerRef.Name)\n   377\u2192\t\t\treturn\n   378\u2192\t\t}\n   379\u2192\n   380\u2192\t\tc.enqueueFoo(foo)\n   381\u2192\t\treturn\n   382\u2192\t}\n   383\u2192}\n   384\u2192\n   385\u2192// newDeployment creates a new Deployment for a Foo resource. tracing documents how controllers register with the controller manager in Kubernetes, following the patterns used by k8s.io/controller-manager (note: this is distinct from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime, though follows similar principles).\\n\\n### Key Components\\n\\n**1. Controller Interface (staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go)**\\nControllers must implement the base `Interface` interface which requires a `Name()` method. Controllers may optionally implement `Debuggable` interface (for debugging handlers) and `HealthCheckable` interface (for health checks).\\n\\n**2. Controller Descriptor Pattern (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:421-429)**\\nUnlike SetupWithManager in controller-runtime, Kubernetes uses a `ControllerDescriptor` struct to register controllers. Each descriptor contains:\\n- Controller name and aliases\\n- InitFunc: a function that creates and initializes the controller\\n- Feature gate requirements\\n- Disabled-by-default flags\\n\\nThis is defined as:\\n```go\\ntype ControllerDescriptor struct {\\n    name                      string\\n    initFunc                  InitFunc\\n    requiredFeatureGates      []featuregate.Feature\\n    aliases                   []string\\n    isDisabledByDefault       bool\\n    isCloudProviderController bool\\n    requiresSpecialHandling   bool\\n}\\n```\\n\\n**3. InitFunc (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:419)**\\nThe InitFunc is the equivalent of SetupWithManager in controller-runtime. It has the signature:\\n```go\\ntype InitFunc func(ctx context.Context, controllerContext ControllerContext, controllerName string) (controller controller.Interface, enabled bool, err error)\\n```\\nThis function is responsible for:\\n- Creating the controller instance\\n- Registering event handlers via informers\\n- Starting the controller's workers\\n- Returning the controller.Interface\\n\\n**4. ControllerContext (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:366-401)**\\nThe ControllerContext is the dependency injection container passed to InitFunc. It provides:\\n- ClientBuilder: for creating Kubernetes API clients\\n- InformerFactory: SharedInformerFactory for accessing informers\\n- ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory: for accessing metadata informers\\n- ComponentConfig: configuration for the controller\\n- RESTMapper: for mapping resources to REST endpoints\\n\\n**5. Reconciliation Pattern (staging/src/k8s.io/endpointslice/reconciler.go)**\\nWhile not using the controller-runtime library, Kubernetes implementations follow a reconciliation pattern. The EndpointSlice reconciler demonstrates this:\\n- A Reconciler struct holds dependencies (clients, listers, etc.)\\n- A Reconcile method transforms current state to desired state\\n- Informer event handlers enqueue items for processing\\n\\n**6. Sample Controller Implementation (staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go)**\\nThe sample controller demonstrates the complete pattern:\\n- NewController() creates the controller, sets up informer event handlers, creates workqueues\\n- Run() starts worker goroutines that process work items\\n- syncHandler performs the actual reconciliation logic\\n- Event handlers call enqueueFoo() to add items to the workqueue\\n\\n### Registration Flow\\n\\n1. **Startup**: kube-controller-manager calls Run() in controllermanager.go:180\\n2. **Descriptor Discovery**: NewControllerDescriptors() returns a map of all available controllers (controllermanager.go:495)\\n3. **Context Creation**: CreateControllerContext() builds the ControllerContext with shared resources (controllermanager.go:228)\\n4. **Controller Initialization**: StartControllers() iterates through descriptors and calls each InitFunc (controllermanager.go:234)\\n5. **Event Handling**: Each controller's InitFunc registers event handlers on informers\\n6. **Worker Loop**: Each controller runs worker goroutines that pull from workqueues\\n7. **Reconciliation**: Workers call syncHandler to bring current state to desired state\\n\\n### Key Differences from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime\\n\\n- **Registration**: ControllerDescriptor + InitFunc vs. SetupWithManager()\\n- **Dependency Injection**: ControllerContext passed explicitly vs. Manager holds references\\n- **Workqueue**: Manually created and managed vs. auto-managed by reconciliation loop\\n- **Event Handler Setup**: Done in InitFunc/NewController vs. done in SetupWithManager\\n- **Reconcile Signature**: Custom per controller vs. standardized Reconcile(ctx, req) -> (Result, error)\\n\\n### Files in the Chain\\n\\nThe registration chain flows through:\\n1. **controllermanager.go:Run()** - Main entry point for the manager\\n2. **controllermanager.go:NewControllerDescriptors()** - Discovers all available controllers\\n3. **controllermanager.go:CreateControllerContext()** - Creates shared dependency container\\n4. **controllermanager.go:StartControllers()** - Initializes all enabled controllers\\n5. **app/core.go, apps.go, batch.go, etc.** - Individual controller InitFunc implementations that call startXxxController()\\n6. **sample-controller/controller.go** - Example of a complete controller implementation\\n\\nThis architecture enables pluggable, independently managed controllers that share common infrastructure like informers, clients, and workqueues.\"\n}\n",

tracing documents how controllers register with the controller manager in Kubernetes, following the patterns used by k8s.io/controller-manager (note: this is distinct from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime, though follows similar principles).\\n\\n### Key Components\\n\\n**1. Controller Interface (staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go)**\\nControllers must implement the base `Interface` interface which requires a `Name()` method. Controllers may optionally implement `Debuggable` interface (for debugging handlers) and `HealthCheckable` interface (for health checks).\\n\\n**2. Controller Descriptor Pattern (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:421-429)**\\nUnlike SetupWithManager in controller-runtime, Kubernetes uses a `ControllerDescriptor` struct to register controllers. Each descriptor contains:\\n- Controller name and aliases\\n- InitFunc: a function that creates and initializes the controller\\n- Feature gate requirements\\n- Disabled-by-default flags\\n\\nThis is defined as:\\n```go\\ntype ControllerDescriptor struct {\\n    name                      string\\n    initFunc                  InitFunc\\n    requiredFeatureGates      []featuregate.Feature\\n    aliases                   []string\\n    isDisabledByDefault       bool\\n    isCloudProviderController bool\\n    requiresSpecialHandling   bool\\n}\\n```\\n\\n**3. InitFunc (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:419)**\\nThe InitFunc is the equivalent of SetupWithManager in controller-runtime. It has the signature:\\n```go\\ntype InitFunc func(ctx context.Context, controllerContext ControllerContext, controllerName string) (controller controller.Interface, enabled bool, err error)\\n```\\nThis function is responsible for:\\n- Creating the controller instance\\n- Registering event handlers via informers\\n- Starting the controller's workers\\n- Returning the controller.Interface\\n\\n**4. ControllerContext (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go:366-401)**\\nThe ControllerContext is the dependency injection container passed to InitFunc. It provides:\\n- ClientBuilder: for creating Kubernetes API clients\\n- InformerFactory: SharedInformerFactory for accessing informers\\n- ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory: for accessing metadata informers\\n- ComponentConfig: configuration for the controller\\n- RESTMapper: for mapping resources to REST endpoints\\n\\n**5. Reconciliation Pattern (staging/src/k8s.io/endpointslice/reconciler.go)**\\nWhile not using the controller-runtime library, Kubernetes implementations follow a reconciliation pattern. The EndpointSlice reconciler demonstrates this:\\n- A Reconciler struct holds dependencies (clients, listers, etc.)\\n- A Reconcile method transforms current state to desired state\\n- Informer event handlers enqueue items for processing\\n\\n**6. Sample Controller Implementation (staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go)**\\nThe sample controller demonstrates the complete pattern:\\n- NewController() creates the controller, sets up informer event handlers, creates workqueues\\n- Run() starts worker goroutines that process work items\\n- syncHandler performs the actual reconciliation logic\\n- Event handlers call enqueueFoo() to add items to the workqueue\\n\\n### Registration Flow\\n\\n1. **Startup**: kube-controller-manager calls Run() in controllermanager.go:180\\n2. **Descriptor Discovery**: NewControllerDescriptors() returns a map of all available controllers (controllermanager.go:495)\\n3. **Context Creation**: CreateControllerContext() builds the ControllerContext with shared resources (controllermanager.go:228)\\n4. **Controller Initialization**: StartControllers() iterates through descriptors and calls each InitFunc (controllermanager.go:234)\\n5. **Event Handling**: Each controller's InitFunc registers event handlers on informers\\n6. **Worker Loop**: Each controller runs worker goroutines that pull from workqueues\\n7. **Reconciliation**: Workers call syncHandler to bring current state to desired state\\n\\n### Key Differences from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime\\n\\n- **Registration**: ControllerDescriptor + InitFunc vs. SetupWithManager()\\n- **Dependency Injection**: ControllerContext passed explicitly vs. Manager holds references\\n- **Workqueue**: Manually created and managed vs. auto-managed by reconciliation loop\\n- **Event Handler Setup**: Done in InitFunc/NewController vs. done in SetupWithManager\\n- **Reconcile Signature**: Custom per controller vs. standardized Reconcile(ctx, req) -> (Result, error)\\n\\n### Files in the Chain\\n\\nThe registration chain flows through:\\n1. **controllermanager.go:Run()** - Main entry point for the manager\\n2. **controllermanager.go:NewControllerDescriptors()** - Discovers all available controllers\\n3. **controllermanager.go:CreateControllerContext()** - Creates shared dependency container\\n4. **controllermanager.go:StartControllers()** - Initializes all enabled controllers\\n5. **app/core.go, apps.go, batch.go, etc.** - Individual controller InitFunc implementations that call startXxxController()\\n6. **sample-controller/controller.go** - Example of a complete controller implementation\\n\\nThis architecture enables pluggable, independently managed controllers that share common infrastructure like informers, clients, and workqueues.\"\n}\n",
